25:T400a3,<p>Questo è stato creato da 1948 Shannon in <a href="https://people.math.harvard.edu/~ctm/home/text/others/shannon/entropy/entropy.pdf">(Shannon 1948)</a>. Questa nozione è basata sulla nozione di probabilità, perché le cose rare sono più informative rispetto a qualcosa che accade spesso.</p>
<h3 id="introduction-to-entropy">Introduction to Entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#introduction-to-entropy">#</a></h3>
<h4 id="the-shannon-information-content">The Shannon Information Content<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#the-shannon-information-content">#</a></h4>
<p>This is dependent on the notion of the <strong>Shannon information content</strong> defined as</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.207em;"><span style="top:-2.4559em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.936em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<p>We will see that the entropy is a weighted average of the information, so the expected information content in a distribution.</p>
<p><a href="/notes/kolmogorov-complexity/">Kolmogorov complexity</a> è un modo diverso per definire la complessità.
Legato è <a href="/notes/neural-networks/#kullback-leibler-divergence">Neural Networks#Kullback-Leibler Divergence</a>.</p>
<p>We can model the classical view of entropy as the from [^1]</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Expected value of <strong>Surprisal</strong> which is the uncertainty of a random variable <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span> taking a certain value which is <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span>, but we want to measure it using log-likelihood.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>With <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&#x3C;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord">∞</span></span></span></span>, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">⋅</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span>.</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord <p>Ossia, possiamo dire in modo intuitivo quanto sarebbe sorprendente vedere che si avverasse quell'evento.</p>

<h4 id="axiomatic-approach-to-entropy">Axiomatic Approach to Entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#axiomatic-approach-to-entropy">#</a></h4>
<p>We can define the entropy as the only function that satisfies the following properties (the function is commonly called <strong>surprise</strong>):</p>
<ol>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span> for every <strong>discrete</strong> r.v. which is related to the code length, which we don't want to be negative</li>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> when <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span></span></span></span> are independent random variables.</li>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord"> is maximal </span></span></span></span></span> when <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∼</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.109em;">U</span><span class="mord mathnormal">ni</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1076em;">f</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> this concept is related to <strong>hard to guess</strong> the results.</li>
</ol>
<p>Then one can prove that the only function that satisfies these properties is the entropy.
Which is:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.3717em;vertical-align:-1.3217em;"></span><span class="mord">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop op-limits"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.05em;"><span style="top:-1.8557em;margin-left:0em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">x</span><span class="mrel mtight">∈</span><span class="mord mathcal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op">∑</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.3217em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<h3 id="properties-of-the-entropy">Properties of the entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#properties-of-the-entropy">#</a></h3>
<p>One observation is that <strong>labels don't matter</strong>, we just need the <em>probability vector</em> and don't care about what it represents.</p>
<p>The entropy is <strong>always positive</strong>. It's easy to prove because all probabilities are <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6835em;vertical-align:-0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&#x3C;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8304em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≤</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span> so every term in the sum is positive because log in that interval is also positive.</p>
<h4 id="axiomatic-approach">Axiomatic approach<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#axiomatic-approach">#</a></h4>
<p>One could derive the entropy from an axiomatic point of view, with the idea of <strong>Surprise</strong>
We just need three requirements:
Given a probability space <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8833em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">Ω</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal">A</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathbb">P</span></span></span></span> , then the surprise of an even <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8193em;vertical-align:-0.136em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">E</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">⊆</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal">A</span></span></span></span> is equal to a function <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">([</span><span class="mord mathbb">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">E</span><span class="mclose">)])</span></span></span></span> which satisfies the following properties:</p>
<ol>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span></li>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span></span></span></span> is continuous</li>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span></span></span></span> is monotonic decreasing, meaning that if <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7335em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.625em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span></span></span></span> then <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&#x3C;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></li>
<li><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span></span></span></span> is additive, meaning that <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">pq</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> when <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.625em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span></span></span></span> are independent.</li>
</ol>
<p>Then we can prove that the only function satisfying these properties has the form:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0576em;">S</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>The entropy is just the expected value of the surprise.</p>
<h4 id="chain-rule">Chain Rule<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#chain-rule">#</a></h4>
<p>non fare.
Una proprietà random è</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>La dimostrazione è abbastanza banale una volta che si conoscono le definizioni....
La cosa interessante è che si può generale per qualunque numero di variabili aleatorie:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="msupsub"><span <h4 id="upper-bound">Upper bound<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#upper-bound">#</a></h4>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≤</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>Con <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span> l'insieme immagine della variabile aleatoria <strong>discreta</strong> <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span>. Importante in questo caso che la nostra variabile sia discreta, altrimenti il teorema provvisto in <a href="https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/book/10.1002/047174882X">(Cover &#x26; Thomas 2012)</a> 2.6.4 non funziona.
Non è molto banale l'idea di utilizzare la uniforme per modellare il numero di elementi. e usare la positività di KL per finire l'upper bound.</p>
<p>We can prove the equality by having an uniform distribution. The computation is easy:
If <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span> is uniform then:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.2574em;vertical-align:-0.936em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.3214em;"><span style="top:-2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.936em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<p>And so we have</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.2574em;vertical-align:-0.936em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.3214em;"><span style="top:-2.314em;"><span class="mclose">∣</span></span></span></span></span>
<p><strong>Proving the upper bound</strong>
Let's take <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.109em;">U</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> into consideration, then we have that this value is</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.6821em;vertical-align:-1.2551em;"></span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op" style="position:relative;top:0em;">∑</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.427em;"><span style="top:-2.2649em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8451em;"><span style="top:-2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mopen mtight">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose mtight">∣</span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.52em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.6em;vertical-align:-0.55em;"></span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op" style="position:relative;top:0em;">∑</span><span class="mspace" class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3283em;"><span style="top:-2.55em;margin-left:-0.1389em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>And by knowing that the Kullback Leibler divergence is positive we know that</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>Which ends the proof.</p>
<h4 id="entropy-is-concave">Entropy is concave<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#entropy-is-concave">#</a></h4>
<p>Uso l'upper bound e il fatto che KL è convesso per dimostrare questa cosa.</p>
<h4 id="functional-dependency">Functional dependency<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#functional-dependency">#</a></h4>
<p>Non fare
Se <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1076em;">f</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> per qualche funzione, allora <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span> si può risolvere con qualche ragionamento sul supporto di entropia.
Interessante vedere che ha una piccola relazione con <a href="/notes/normalizzazione-dei-database/#dipendenze-funzionali">Normalizzazione dei database#Dipendenze funzionali</a>.</p>
<h4 id="monotonicity-of-entropy">Monotonicity of Entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#monotonicity-of-entropy">#</a></h4>
<p>This theorem states that</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>It is also called the principle <em>Information never hurts</em> meaning you are never more uncertain about a random variable when you have more information about it.</p>
<p>It's easy to see why its true!</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" <h3 id="types-of-entropy">Types of entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#types-of-entropy">#</a></h3>

<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span <p>La nozione con il valore atteso è la più semplice anche in questo caso.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>conditional entropy corresponds to the expected remaining uncertainty in <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span></span></span></span> after we observe <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span></span></span></span></p>
</blockquote>
<p>We can also express conditional entropy as</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.4em;vertical-align:-0.95em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbb">E</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.5198em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mopen mtight">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">x</span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" mtight">)</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" class="mclose delimcenter" style="top:0em;"><span class="delimsizing size3">]</span></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<h4 id="joint-entropy">Joint Entropy<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#joint-entropy">#</a></h4>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.4361em;vertical-align:-1.3861em;"></span><span class="mord">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop op-limits"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.05em;"><span style="top:-1.9em;margin-left:0em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">x</span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op">∑</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.3861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>We observe that there is a relation between Joint entropy and the conditional entropy:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0785em;">X</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" class="mrel">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.2222em;">Y</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<h3 id="relative-entropy-or-kullback-leibler">Relative Entropy or Kullback-Leibler<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#relative-entropy-or-kullback-leibler">#</a></h3>
<p>Let's take
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">∣</span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mclose">∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&#x3C;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord">∞</span></span></span></span>, and take distributions P, Q, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">→</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6889em;"></span><span class="mord mathbb">R</span></span></span></span> such that  <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7335em;vertical-align:-0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord">0∀</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span> and the sum is 1, same thing for <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span>, then we define the Kullback-Leibler Divergence between those distributions to be</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:2.7487em;vertical-align:-1.3217em;"></span><span class="mop op-limits"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.05em;"><span style="top:-1.8557em;margin-left:0em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">x</span><span class="mrel mtight">∈</span><span class="mord mathcal mtight" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3.05em;"></span><span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op">∑</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.3217em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.427em;"><span style="top:-2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.936em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span>
<p>We need to define some corner cases:</p>
<ul>
<li>If <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span> is anything then its 0</li>
<li>If <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">∃</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.046em;">ξ</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathcal" style="margin-right:0.1464em;">X</span></span></span></span> such that <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.046em;">ξ</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.046em;">ξ</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span> => <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6667em;vertical-align:-0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">+</span><span class="mord">∞</span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li>If <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.7224em;vertical-align:-0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≪</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span> then <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">&#x3C;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord">∞</span></span></span></span> (I did not understand why)</li>
</ul>
<p>This has some relations with the entropy, we can use some log properties and have the following result:</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">−</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0813em;">H</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.6em;vertical-align:-0.55em;"></span><span class="mop op-symbol large-op" style="position:relative;top:0em;">∑</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>The second addendum can be called <em>cross-entropy</em>.</p>
<p>In modo praticamente equivalente possiamo definire una versione condizionata. e si può applicare anche in questo caso una chain rule</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">))</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mord">∣</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">y</span><span class="mclose">))</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>Relative entropy <strong>is not a distance</strong> not a metric, so its incorrect to say it is a distance, but for practical purposes it seems to work well: if the Relative entropy is small also the probability vectors are small.</p>
<h4 id="kl-is-positive-or-null">KL is positive or null<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#kl-is-positive-or-null">#</a></h4>
<p>Ossia per ogni distribuzione <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.625em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span></span></span></span> o <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.625em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span></span></span></span> si ha che</p>
<span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">≥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span></span>
<p>Con uguaglianza se hanno esattamente la stessa distribuzione.
We have that <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6684em;vertical-align:-0.024em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">⟺</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.1389em;">P</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8778em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span> .</p>
<p>E ricordandoci che <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8889em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mop">lo<span style="margin-right:0.0139em;">g</span></span></span></span></span> è una funzione concava, quindi si può utilizzare <a href="/notes/analisi-di-convessita/#jensen">Jensen</a>.
Lo dimostriamo ora in breve.
Sappiamo che la funzione <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span <p>In modo facile.</p>
<h4 id="kl-is-convex">KL is convex<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#kl-is-convex">#</a></h4>
<p><span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0278em;">D</span><span class="mord mathnormal">L</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∣∣</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> è convesso sulla coppia <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">p</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0359em;">q</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span>, 2.7.2 di <a href="https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/book/10.1002/047174882X">(Cover &#x26; Thomas 2012)</a>.
Anche sula 2.26 di McKay è buono, anche se non esattamente parla di questo.</p>
<h4 id="relationship-with-chi2-divergence">Relationship with <span class="katex"><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.0085em;vertical-align:-0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8141em;"><span style="top:-3.063em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>-divergence.<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#relationship-with-chi2-divergence">#</a></h4>
<p>Chi-squared divergence — χ²(P‖Q) = ∫ (p(x)−q(x))²/q(x) dx = E_q[(p/q)²] − 1 — is an f-divergence with f(t) = (t−1)². It sits in an interesting relationship with KL: it upper bounds KL (KL(P‖Q) ≤ log(1+χ²(P‖Q)) ≤ χ²(P‖Q)), and locally both reduce to the Fisher information metric to leading order.</p>
<p><strong>Pros</strong></p>
<p><em>Stronger divergence, better bounds.</em> Because χ² dominates KL, minimizing it gives you a KL bound for free. This shows up usefully in PAC-Bayes (Catoni-style bounds), DRO (Duchi–Namkoong's chi-squared uncertainty balls have clean duals and finite-sample guarantees), and in CHIVI (Dieng et al. 2017), where you get an <em>upper</em> bound on log evidence — complementing the ELBO's lower bound so you can sandwich it.</p>
<p><em>Direct variance interpretation.</em> χ²(p‖q) is the variance of the importance ratio p/q (up to the −1). So if your downstream use of q is importance sampling — off-policy RL, Monte Carlo estimation, self-normalized estimators — chi-squared minimization is <em>literally</em> variance minimization on the estimator. KL doesn't give you that.</p>
<p><em>More mode-covering (in the forward direction).</em> Reverse KL is famously mode-seeking; forward KL is mean-seeking but logarithmically forgiving of mass-coverage failures. Chi-squared penalizes those failures quadratically, so it pushes harder to cover tails of p.</p>
<p><em>Doesn't require log-densities.</em> Useful when you only have unnormalized densities or numerically fragile log-probs, and in some f-GAN-style objectives. LSGAN is essentially a chi-squared variant.</p>
<p><em>Robustness properties.</em> Chi-squared-regularized policy optimization has been shown to be more robust to model misspecification than KL-regularized versions in some RL settings — related to its DRO interpretation.</p>
<p><strong>Cons</strong></p>
<p><em>Catastrophically high-variance estimators.</em> This is the big one. The integrand involves p²/q, so whenever q assigns low probability where p doesn't, the Monte Carlo estimator explodes. KL with its log ratio is far more numerically forgiving. In practice this is why chi-squared methods often fail to scale.</p>
<p><em>Exponential blow-up with dimension.</em> KL is additive over independent factors: KL(p₁p₂‖q₁q₂) = KL(p₁‖q₁) + KL(p₂‖q₂). Chi-squared is <em>multiplicative</em>: 1+χ² = (1+χ²₁)(1+χ²₂). So for d independent dims with per-dim χ² = c, the joint χ² is (1+c)^d − 1. For high-dimensional models (sequences, images, multi-agent state spaces) this is a real problem.</p>
<p><em>No MLE interpretation.</em> Forward KL minimization is maximum likelihood, which gives you all of statistical learning theory for free. Chi-squared minimization is a different estimator — consistent, but without the same asymptotic and finite-sample machinery.</p>
<p><em>Loses the exponential-family / Bregman structure.</em> KL between exponential families is a Bregman divergence with closed forms; gradients and natural gradients have clean expressions. Chi-squared lacks this, so you give up a lot of conjugacy and tractability.</p>
<p><em>Less mature tooling and theory.</em> Most autodiff frameworks, RL algorithms, and VI methods are built around KL/cross-entropy. Convergence theory, hyperparameter heuristics, and best practices are far thinner for chi-squared, so you're often doing more methodological work yourself.</p>
<p><em>Sensitive to support mismatch.</em> If p has any mass where q is zero, χ² is infinite — same as KL — but the quadratic penalty makes near-zero q values numerically catastrophic well before you hit the singularity.</p>
<p><strong>When it's actually worth it</strong></p>
<p>Roughly: when you specifically care about variance of importance weights (off-policy estimation, sequential Monte Carlo), when you need an upper bound on log evidence (CHIVI), when you want DRO guarantees, or in low-dimensional problems where the variance and dimensionality issues don't bite. For typical large-scale training — RLHF, VI on neural nets, language modeling — KL's numerical behavior and additivity make it the default for good reasons, and chi-squared mostly shows up as a regularizer or auxiliary term rather than the primary objective.</p>
<h3 id="mutual-information">Mutual information<a class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" hidden href="#mutual-information">#</a></h3>
<p>Questa nozione definisce quanta informazione hanno in comune due variabili aleatorie</p>

style="margin-right:0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal"
